<thinking>**Timestamp parsing error**
The error occurs when trying to parse a timestamp that contains 'Z' (UTC indicator). The issue is that `workspace.source_metadata.timestamp` might already be a datetime object, not a string, or the replace operation is failing. I need to check the workspace_state.py to see how timestamps are stored and handle this more robustly.

<thinking>**Timestamp parsing error**

The error occurs at line 1239 where we're trying to parse a timestamp. The issue is that `workspace.source_metadata.timestamp` is already a `datetime` object (as defined in `workspace_state.py` line 35: `timestamp: datetime`), but the code is trying to call `.replace()` on it as if it were a string.

The fix is to check if it's already a datetime object or handle it properly.

## Bob Shell

Timestamp: 2026-05-16T17:44:09.040Z

Model: premium

<thinking>**Fix timestamp parsing error**

The error occurs because `workspace.source_metadata.timestamp` is a `datetime` object (as defined in `SourceMetadata` dataclass), not a string. The code was trying to call `.replace()` on a datetime object, which doesn't have that method.

I've fixed it by:
1. Checking if `ts` is a string first before trying to parse it
2. If it's already a datetime object, use it directly
3. Added AttributeError to the exception handling for safety

The fix handles both cases:
- When timestamp is a datetime object (normal case from `SourceMetadata.from_snapshot`)
- When timestamp might be a string (edge case from deserialization)
</thinking>
